< Text>
What was intended to be a simple tire purchase and installation mutated into an attempt to upsell me on unnecessary and expensive work using fear tactics.
I had used Big O Tires' website to get a quote and schedule an appointment. The selected tires offered a promotional deal to knock off $100 from the original price and include installation as well as an alignment check. Simple enough.
Fast forward to the appointment day: the car is dropped off and about an hour or so after, they tell me over the phone that it needs a new axle, rotors and brake pads, and the shocks should all be replaced. Unless I get the axle and brakes handled immediately, I'm going to have major issues. I say no to all of that. Then I'm told the price of everything else. They disregarded the promotion AND tacked on an actual alignment without asking first. Trying to sneak in some extra charges? Not with me.
After I explained that this wasn't the deal, they added the original promotion code and removed the cost of the alignment.
I took my car to a mechanic I trust and he told me "come back in a few months to get your brakes done. Your car is fine." He could have told me to get the work done with him, but he's an honest person.
Tire shop mechanics commonly work off of commission, so they'll take every chance they can in order to upsell you. Some drivers that are not so well versed with vehicles may be more prone to their methods. Max didn't push me very hard, but trying to upsell meat at all on a ton of work to get an extra $2k is frustrating. Telling me that bearings are about to pop out and the rear brakes are grinding, when this has been disproven by another mechanic is infuriating.
If you're still considering Big O Tires just to buy tires, they have competitive deals. There's no doubt about that. However, tell them to just deal with the tires and leave everything else alone. Be firm about it. Then find a local mechanic you can trust.
Big O Tires: never again.<//Text>

First California requires an utlra low NOx tank, this tank is more expensive than water heaters sold outside of the state and has fewer emissions than water heaters sold in other states. <UserId.>110521733579156618339</UserId.>< Review>
We've come to Tpumps a couple of times now and will continue to check out the many different types of combos we can make for these teas(the name of the place says it all people lol pumps). Now I'm not a big fan of boba lol but these weren't bad, well at least the honey one's I haven't tried the others. I liked the fact that they let us try it before putting it in our cups.
Each time we've come we were offered free samples of different teas which have been good. The milk one wasn't bad either, first time trying it too.
You do have to have some patience, they only have one register but once you place you're drink order the rest of the process moves pretty quickly. So yes, you will most of the time find the line out the door.</Review>
